Since such a high-performance server consumes a large amount of current during operation and generates a lot \nof heat to deteriorate the operation environment, high reliability of the components is required. CPU power line consuming a large \namount of currents requires many small-sized and high-capacitance MLCCs to lower the impedance, and the components for high-\ntemperature in the high-temperature environment around CPU.\n333 3\n3\nVoltage Regulator\nAC-DC Power ModuleCPU#0 CPU#1DIMM (Bank1)\nSocket\nSocketDIMM (Bank2)\nDIMM (Bank2)DIMM (Bank1)\n11\n1 4 4 2 2PCIe\nPCIe\nPCIe\nPCIe\nNoise Filtering, \nStable Power \nDeliveryHigh Bending\nStrengthMiddle & High\nFreq. With the introduction of 5G, high-integrated and high-performance FPGA/DSP are being used for network \nequipment to cope with the demand of faster data processing speed and to process the data traffic surge. Reliability test Condition - Capacitance” in this document.\n The following table shows the voltage and frequency condition ac cording to the capacitance range.  \n [The voltage and frequency condition according to MLCC the capacitance range]\nTan δ (DF)2\nＩ. \u200c\u200cAn ideal MLCC’s energy loss is zero, but real MLCC has dielectric loss and resistance loss of electrode. DF (Dissipation F actor) \nis defined as the ratio of loss energy to stored energy and typically being calculated as percentage.\nⅡ. \u200c\u200cQuality factor (Q factor) is defined as the ratio of stored energy to loss energy. The equation can be described as 1/\nDF. Normally the loss characteristic of Class Ⅰ MLCC is presented in Q, since the DF value is so small whereas the loss \ncharacteristic of Class Ⅱ MLCC is presented in DF.\nⅢ. \u200c\u200cIt is recommended to use Class Ⅰ MLCC for applications to require good linearity and low loss such as coupling circuit, filter \ncircuit and time constant circuit.Ⅱ. \u200c\u200cIt is recommended to use measurement equipment with the ALC (Auto Level Control) option.  \nThe reason is that when capacitance or measurement frequency is high, the output voltage of measurement equipment can \nbe lower than the setting voltage due to the equipment limitation. Note that when capacitance or measurement frequency \nis excessively high, the measurement equipment may show ALC off warning and provide a lower output voltage than the \nsetting voltage even with ALC option selected. It is necessary to ensure the output voltage of measurement equipment is the \nsame as the setting voltage before measuring capacitance.\nⅢ. \u200c\u200cCapacitance value of high dielectric constant (Class Ⅱ) MLCC changes with applied AC and DC voltage. Therefore, it is \nnecessary to take into account MLCC’s AC voltage characteristics and DC-bias voltage characteristics when applying MLCC to \nthe actual circuit.\nⅣ. \u200c\u200cThe capacitance is in compliance with the EIA RS-198-1-F-2002.ClassⅠ\nCapacitance Frequency Voltage\n≤1,000㎊ 1㎒±10%\n0.5~5Vrms\n>1,000㎊ 1㎑±10%ClassⅡ\nCapacitance Frequency Voltage\n≤10㎌ 1㎑±10% 1.0±0.2Vrms\n>10㎌ 120㎐±20% 0.5±0.1Vrms\nException 1㎑±10% 0.5±0.1Vrms\n※   Capacitance shall be measured after the heat treatment of 150+0/-\n10℃ for 1hr, leaving at room temperature for 24±2hr. It is also necessary to \nconsider the aging characteristic with voltage and temperature characteristics when Class Ⅱ MLCC is used in circuitry.\nＩ. \u200c\u200cIn general, aging causes capacitance to decrease linearly with the log of time as shown in the following graph. Please check \nwith SEMCO for more details, since the value may vary between different models.\nⅡ. \u200c\u200cAfter heat treatment (150 °C, 1hour), the capacitance decreased by aging is recovered, so aging should be considered again \nfrom the time of heat treatment. Insulation Resistance3\nCeramic dielectric has a low leakage current with DC voltage due to the high insulating properties.  \nInsulation resistance is defined as the ratio of a leakage current to DC voltage. \nＩ. \u200c\u200cWhen applying DC voltage to MLCC, a charging current and a leakage current flow together at the initial stage of \nmeasurement. \n While the charging current decreases, and insulation resistance (IR ) in MLCC is saturated by time.  \n Therefore, insulation resistance shall be measured 1 minute after applying the rated voltage.\n1Capacitance Change(%)\nTime(h)10 100 1,000 10,000 100,000C0G\nX7R\nX5R\n[Example of Capacitance Aging]* Sample : C0G, X7R, X5R\n108\nMULTILAYER CERAMIC CAPACITORS\nReliability Test Conditions\nPackaging Specifications\n\t Caution/Notice\nDisclaimer & Limitation of Use and Applications\nComponent sales offices/manufacturing \u200c\nsites\nCaution/NoticeEmbedded/LSC Capacitors\nHigh Bending Strength Capacitors\nLow Acoustic Noise Capacitors\nLow ESL Capacitors\nArray Type Capacitors\nApplication Guide Explanation of Ceramic Capacitors\nPart Numbering\nReliability Level Description\nNormal Capacitors_Standard\nNormal Capacitors_High Level Ⅰ\nNormal Capacitors_High Level  Ⅱ\nTemperature Characteristics of Capacitance (TCC)5\nPlease consider temperature characteristics of capacitance since the electrical characteristics such as capacitance changes which \nis caused by a change in ceramic dielectric constant by temperature.\nＩ. \u200c\u200cIt is necessary to check the values specified in section “C. Reliability test Condition–T emperature Characteristics” for the \ntemperature and capacitance change range of MLCC.\nSelf-heating Temperature6\nIt is necessary to design the system, with considering self-heating generated by the ESR (Equivalent Series Resistance) of MLCC \nwhen AC voltage or pulse voltage is applied to MLCC.\nＩ. \u200c\u200cWhen MLCC is used in an AC voltage or pulse voltage  \ncircuit, self-heating is generated when AC or pulse  \ncurrent flows through MLCC. Short-circuit may be  \noccurred by the degradation of MLCC’s insulating  \nproperties.\nⅡ. \u200c\u200cThe reliability of MLCC may be affected by MLCC being used  \nin an AC voltage or pulse voltage circuit, even the AC voltage  \nor the pulse voltage is within the range of rated voltage.  \nTherefore, make sure to check the following conditions.\n1)   The surface temperature of MLCC must stay within  \nthe maximum operating temperature after AC or  \nPulse voltage is applied. \n2)   The rise in increase by self-heating of MLCC must not  \nexceed 20℃Ⅱ. \u200c\u200cWhen selecting MLCC, it is necessary to consider the heat characteristics of a system, room temperature and T CC of MLCC, \nsince the applied temperature may change the capacitance of MLCC.\nⅢ. \u200c\u200cIn addition, Bias TCC of MLCC should be taken into account when DC voltage is applied to MLCC.[Example of Temperature Characteristics (X5R)] [Example of Bias TCC]* Sample : 10uF, Rated voltage 6.3V * Sample : 10uF, Rated required to consider voltage characteristics in the circuit since the capacitance value of high dielectric constant MLCC (Class Ⅱ) \nis changed by applied DC & AC voltage.\nＩ. \u200c\u200cPlease ensure the capacitance change is within the allowed operating range of a system. In particular, when high dielectric \nconstant type MLCC (Class Ⅱ) is used in circuit with narrow allowed capacitance tolerance, a system should be designed with \nconsidering DC voltage, temperature characteristics and aging characteristics of MLCC.\nⅡ. \u200c\u200cIt is necessary to consider the AC voltage characteristics of MLCC and the AC voltage of a system, since the capacitance value \nof high dielectric constant type MLCC (Class Ⅱ) varies with the applied AC voltage.\n[Example of DC Bias characteristics] [Example of AC voltage characteristics]* Sample : X5R 10uF, Rated voltage 6.3V * Sample : X5R 10uF, Rated voltage 6.3V40\n30\n20\n10\n0\n-10\n-20\n-30\n-40\n0.0 0.5 1.0 1.5 2.0ΔC(%)\nAC Voltage(Vrms)20\n0\n-20\n-40\n-60\n-80\n-100\n0 1 2 3 4 5 6ΔC(%)\nDC Voltage(V)\n110\nMULTILAYER CERAMIC CAPACITORS\nReliability Test Conditions\nPackaging Specifications\n\t Caution/Notice\nDisclaimer & Limitation of Use and Applications\nComponent sales offices/manufacturing \u200c\nsites\nCaution/NoticeEmbedded/LSC Capacitors\nHigh Bending Strength Capacitors\nLow Acoustic Noise Capacitors\nLow ESL Capacitors\nArray Type Capacitors\nApplication Guide Explanation of Ceramic Capacitors\nPart Numbering\nReliability Level Description\nNormal Capacitors_Standard\nNormal Capacitors_High Level Ⅰ\nNormal Capacitors_High Level  Ⅱ\nⅡ. \u200c\u200cMLCC operates as an inductor in the high frequency \nand the inductance of MLCC is called ESL (Equivalent \nSeries Inductance). The reactance (XL) of MLCC in the \nhigh frequency increases as frequency increases ( X_\nL=j2πf·ESL ). The resistance (ESR) of MLCC in the high \nfrequency mainly comes from the loss of its electrode \nmetal.\nⅢ. \u200c\u200cSRF (Self Resonant Frequency) of MLCC is the frequency \nwhere its capacitive reactance (XC) and inductive \nreactance(XL) cancel each other and the impedance of \nMLCC has only ESR at SRF. \nⅣ. \u200c\u200cThe impedance of MLCC can be measured by a network \nanalyzer or an impedance analyzer. When using the \nnetwork analyzer, please note that the small-signal input \nmay lead to the impedance of low capacitance caused \nby the AC voltage characteristic of MLCC.[Example of Impedance characteristics]* Sample : X5R 1uF, Rated voltage 6.3V100\n10\n1\n0.1\n0.01\n0.01 0.1 1 10 100 1000 10000lZl, ESR(Ohm)\nFrequency(㎒)Impedance IZI, ESR\n(Capacitor region) (Inductor region)\nSRF\nlZl\nESRImpedance Characteristic8\nElectrical impedance (Z) of MLCC is the measurement of the opposition that MLCC presents to a current (I) when a voltage (V) is \napplied. It is defined as the ratio of the voltage to the current (Z=V/I).  \nImpedance extends the concept of resistance to AC circuits and is a complex number consisting of the real part of resistance (R) \nand the imaginary part of reactance (X) as Z=R+jX. \nTherefore, it is required to design circuit with consideration of the impedance characteristics of MLCC based on the frequency \n(Z=R+jX)\nＩ. \u200c\u200cMLCC operates as a capacitor in the low frequency and its reactance (XC) decreases as frequency increases ( X_C=1/j2πfC ) \nwhere f is frequency and C is capacitance.  \nThe resistance (ESR; Equivalent Series Resistance) of MLCC in the low frequency mainly comes from the loss of its dielectric \nmaterial.\n111\nMULTILAYER CERAMIC CAPACITORS\nReliability Test Conditions\nPackaging Specifications\n\t Caution/Notice\nDisclaimer & Limitation of Use and Applications\nComponent sales offices/manufacturing \u200c\nsites\nCaution/NoticeEmbedded/LSC Capacitors\nHigh Bending Strength Capacitors\nLow Acoustic Noise Capacitors\nLow ESL Capacitors\nArray Type Capacitors\nApplication Guide Explanation of Ceramic Capacitors\nPart Numbering\nReliability Level Description\nNormal Capacitors_Standard\nNormal Capacitors_High Level Ⅰ\nNormal Capacitors_High Level  Ⅱ\nElectrical & Mechanical Caution\nDerating1\nMLCC with the test voltage at 100% of the rated voltage in the high temperature resistance test are labeled as “derated MLCC.” \nFor this type of MLCC, the voltage and temperature should be derated as shown in the following graph for the equivalent life \ntime of a normal MLCC with the test voltage at 150% of the rated voltage in the high temperature resistance test.\nＩ. \u200c\u200cThe derated MLCC should be applied with the derating \nvoltage and temperature as shown in the following \ngraph.\nⅡ. \u200c\u200cThe “Temperature of MLCC” in the x-axis of the graph \nbelow indicates the surface temperature of MLCC \nincluding self-heating effect. Effect of EOS (Electrical Overstress)\n   Electrical Overstress such as a surge voltage or EOS can cause damages to MLCC, resulting in the electrical short failure \ncaused by the dielectric breakdown in MLCC.\n   Down time of MLCC is varied with the applied voltage and the room temperature and a dielectric shock caused by EOS can \naccelerate heating on the dielectric. Therefore, it can bring about a failure of MLCC in a market at the early stage. \n   Please use caution not to apply excessive electrical overstress including spike voltage MLCC when preparing MLCC for \ntesting or evaluating.\n(1) Surge\nWhen the overcurrent caused by surge is applied to MLCC, the influx of current into MLCC can induce the overshooting \nphenomenon of voltage as shown in the graph below and result in the electrical short failure in MLCC. Therefore, it is \nnecessary to be careful to prevent the influx of surge current into MLCC.\n(2) ESD (Electrostatic Discharge)\nSince the voltage of the static electricity is very high but the quantity of electric charge is small compared to the surge, ESD \ncan cause damage to MLCC with low capacitance as shown in the following graph, whereas surge with lots of electric \ncharge quantity can cause damages to even high capacitance MLCC.\n113\nMULTILAYER CERAMIC CAPACITORS\nReliability Test Conditions\nPackaging Specifications\n\t Caution/Notice\nDisclaimer & Limitation of Use and Applications\nComponent sales offices/manufacturing \u200c\nsites\nCaution/NoticeEmbedded/LSC Capacitors\nHigh Bending Strength Capacitors\nLow Acoustic Noise Capacitors\nLow ESL Capacitors\nArray Type Capacitors\nApplication Guide Explanation of Ceramic Capacitors\nPart Numbering\nReliability Level Description\nNormal Capacitors_Standard\nNormal Capacitors_High Level Ⅰ\nNormal Capacitors_High Level  Ⅱ\nProcess of Mounting and Soldering\nMounting1\nMLCC with the test voltage at 100% of the rated voltage in the high temperature resistance test are labeled as “derated MLCC.” \nFor this type of MLCC, the voltage and temperature should be derated as shown in the following graph for the equivalent life \ntime of a normal MLCC with the test voltage at 150% of the rated voltage in the high temperature resistance test.\nＩ. \u200c\u200cMounting position\n It is recommended to locate the major axis of MLCC in parallel to the direction in which the stress is applied.\nⅡ. \u200c\u200cCautions during mounting near the cutout\nPlease take the following measures to effectively reduce the stress generated from the cutting of PCB. Optimum solder flux for reflow soldering\n   Overly the thick application of solder pastes results in an excessive solder fillet height.\n   This makes MLCC more vulnerable to the mechanical and thermal stress from the board, which may cause cracks in MLCC.\n   Too little solder paste results in a lack of the adhesive strength, which may cause MLCC to isolate from PCB\n   Check if solder has been applied uniformly after soldering is completed.\n   It is required to design a PCB with consideration of a solder land pattern and its size to apply an appropriate amount of \nsolder to MLCC. How to use a soldering Iron\n   In order to minimize damages on MLCC, preheating MLCC and PCB is necessary.\n   A hot plate and a hot air type preheater should be used for preheating\n   Do not cool down MLCC and PCB rapidly after soldering.\n   Keep the contact time between the outer termination of MLCC and the soldering iron as short as possible. Long soldering \ntime may cause problems such as adhesion deterioration by the leaching phenomenon of the outer termination.Soldering Iron6\nⅡ.  How to use a spot heater\nCompared to local heating using a solder iron, heat by a spot heater heats the overall MLCC and the PCB, which is likely to \nlessen the thermal shocks.  \nFor a high density PCB, a spot heater can prevent the problem to connect between a solder iron and MLCC directly. \n   If the distance from the air nozzle outlet to MLCC is too close, MLCC may be cracked due to the thermal stress. Cautions for re-work\n   Too much solder amount will increase the risk of PCB \nbending or cause other damages. \n   Too little solder amount will result in MLCC breaking loose \nfrom the PCB due to the inadequate adhesive strength.\n   Check if the solder has been applied properly and ensure \nthe solder fillet has a proper shape.\n Confirm the position of the support pin or jig when checking the electrical performance of MLCC after mounting on the PCB.\n Watch for PCB bending caused by the pressure of a test-probe or other equipment.\n If the PCB is bent by the force from the test probe, MLCC may be cracked or the solder joint may be damaged.\n Avoid PCB flexing by using the support pin on the back side of the PCB.\n Place equipment with the support pin as close to the test-probe as possible. \n Prevent shock vibrations of the board when the test-probe contacts a PCB.Cautions for using electrical measuring probes8Ｉ. \u200c\u200cIn general, cleaning is unnecessary if rosin flux is used.  \nWhen acidic flux is used strongly, chlorine in the flux may dissolve into some types of cleaning fluids, thereby affecting the \nperformance of MLCC.  \nThis means that the cleansing solution must be carefully selected and should always be new.\nⅡ. Requirements for Adhesives\n They must have enough adhesive strength to prevent MLCC from slipping or moving during the handling the board.\n They must maintain their adhesive strength when exposed to soldering temperatures.\n They should not spread when applied to the PCB.\n They should have a long pot life.\n They should hardened quickly.\n They should not corrode the board or MLCC materials.\n They should be an insulator type that does not affect the characteristic of MLCC.\n They should be non-toxic, not harmful, and particularly safe when workers touch the adhesives.\nⅡ.  Caution before Applying Adhesive\nCheck the correct application conditions before attaching MLCC to the board with an adhesive. \nIf the dimension of land, the type of adhesives, the amount of coating, the contact surface areas, the curing temperature, or \nother conditions are not appropriate, it may degrade the MLCC performance.\nⅢ.  Cautions for selecting Adhesive \nDepending on the type of the chosen adhesive, MLCC insulation resistance may be degraded. \nIn addition, MLCC may be cracked by the difference in contractile stress caused by the different contraction rate between \nMLCC and the adhesive.\nⅣ.  Cautions for the amount of applied adhesive and curing temperature\n   The inappropriate amount of the adhesive cause the weak adhesive strength, resulting in the mounting defect in MLCC.\n   Excessive use of the adhesive may cause a soldering defect, loss of electrical connection, incorrect curing, or slippage of a \nmounting position, thereby an inflow of the adhesive onto the land section should be avoided.\n   If the curing temperature is too high or the curing time is too long, the adhesive strength will be degraded. In addition, \noxidation both on the outer termination (Sn) of MLCC and the surface of the board may deteriorate the solderability.Adhesive selection11\nFlux12\nＩ. \u200c\u200cThe excessive amount of flux generates excessive flux gases which may deteriorate solderability. Therefore, apply the flux thin \nand evenly as a whole.\nⅡ. \u200c\u200cFlux with a high ratio of halogen may oxidize the outer termination of MLCC, if cleaning is not done properly. Therefore, use \nflux with a halogen content of 0.1% max.\nⅢ. \u200c\u200cStrong acidic flux can degrade the MLCC performance.\nⅣ. \u200c\u200cCheck the solder quality of MLCC and the amount of remaining flux surrounding MLCC after the mounting process.\n123\nMULTILAYER CERAMIC CAPACITORS\nReliability Test Conditions\nPackaging Specifications\n\t Caution/Notice\nDisclaimer & Limitation of Use and Applications\nComponent sales offices/manufacturing \u200c\nsites\nCaution/NoticeEmbedded/LSC Capacitors\nHigh Bending Strength Capacitors\nLow Acoustic Noise Capacitors\nLow ESL Capacitors\nArray Type Capacitors\nApplication Guide Explanation of Ceramic Capacitors\nPart Numbering\nReliability Level Description\nNormal Capacitors_Standard\nNormal Capacitors_High Level Ⅰ\nNormal Capacitors_High Level  Ⅱ\nCoating13\nＩ. \u200c\u200cCrack caused by Coating\n   A crack may be caused in the MLCC due to amount of the resin and stress of thermal contraction of the resin during coating \nprocess.\n During the coating process, the amount of resin and the stress of t hermal contraction of the resin may cause cracks in MLCC.\n   The difference of thermal expansion coefficient between the coati ng, or a molding resin may cause destruction, deterioration \nof insulation resistance or dielectric breakdown of MLCC such as cracks or detachment, etc.\nⅡ.  Recommended Coating material\n A therm al expansion coefficient should be as close to that of MLCC as possible.\n A silicone resin can be used as an under-coating to buffer the stress.\n The resin should have a minimum curing contraction rate.\n The resin should have a minimum sensitivity (ex. Epoxy resin).\n   The insulation resistance of MLCC can be deteriorated if a high hygroscopic property resin is used in a high humidity \ncondition.\n   Do not use strong acid substances due to the fact that coating materials inducing a family of halogen substances and \norganic acid may corrode MLCC. \nDesign\nCircuit design1\nWhen the board is dropped or bent, MLCC mounted on the board may be short-circuited by the drop in insulation resistance. \nTherefore, it is required to install safety equipment such as a fuse to prevent additional accidents when MLCC is short-circuited, \notherwise, electric short and fire may occur. This product is not a safety guaranteed product..\nPCB Design2\nＩ. \u200c\u200cUnlike lead type components, SMD type components that are designed to be mounted directly on the board are fragile to the \nstress. In addition, they are more sensitive to mechanical and thermal stress than lead type components. \nⅡ.  MLCC crack by PCB material type\nA great difference of the thermal expansion coefficient between PCB and MLCC causes thermal expansion and contraction, \nresulting in cracks in MLCC. Even though MLCC is mounted on a board with a fluorine resin or on a single-layered glass epoxy, \ncracks in MLCC may occur.\nDesign system evaluation3\nＩ. \u200c\u200cEvaluate the actual design with MLCC to make sure there is no functional issue or violation of specifications of the finished \ngoods.\nⅡ.    Please note that the capacitance may differ based on the operating condition of the actual system since Class 2 MLCC \ncapacitance varies with applied voltage and temperature. \nⅢ.    Surge resistance must be evaluated since the excessive surge caused by the inductance of the actual system may apply to \nMLCC.\nⅣ. Recommendation for temperature/humidity\n   E v en taping and packaging materials are designed to endure a long-term storage, they should be stored with a temperature \nof 0~40°C and an RH of 0~70% otherwise, too high temperatures or humidity may deteriorate the quality of the product \nrapidly.\n   As oxidization is accelerated when relative humidity is above 70%R H, the lower the humidity is, the better the solderability is.\n   As the temperature difference may cause dew condensation during the storage of the product, it is a must to maintain a \ntemp erature control environment.\nⅡ. Shelf Life\nAn allowable  storage period should be within 6 months from the outgoing date of delivery in consideration of solderability. \nAs for produc ts in storage over 6 months, please check solderability before use.\nCaution for corrosive environment2\nAs corrosive gases may deteriorate the solderability of MLCC outer termination, it is a must to store MLCC in an environment \nwithout gases. MLCC that is exposed to corrosive gases may cause its quality issues due to the corrosion of plating layers and the \npenetration of moisture.\nWaste treatment4\nIn case of scrapping MLCC, it is incinerated or buried by a licensed industrial waste company. When scrapping MLCC, it is \nrecommended to incinerate or bury the scrappage by a licensed industrial waste company.Equipment in operation3\nＩ. Do not touch MLCC directly with bare hands to prevent an electric shock or damage. \nⅡ. \u200c\u200cThe termination of MLCC shall not be contacted with a conductive object (short –circuit). Do not expose MLCC to conductive \nliquid containing acidic or alkaline material.\nⅢ. \u200c\u200cDo not use the equipment in the following conditions.\n(1) Exposure to water or oil\n(2) Exposure to direct sunlight\n(3) Exposure to Ozone or ultra-violet radiation.\n(4) Exposure to corrosive gas (e.g. hydrogen sulfide, sulfur dioxide, chlorine, ammonia gas)\n(5) Exposure to vibration or mechanical shock exceeding specified limit\n(6) Exposure to high humidity\nⅣ. \u200c\u200cIf the equipment starts generating any smoke, fire or smell, immediately switch it off or unplug from the power source.  \nIf the equipment is not switched off or unplugged, serious damage may occur due to the continuous power supply. ### Component Summary for CL21B392KBANNNC (Samsung)

#### Key Characteristics and Specifications:
- **Type**: Multilayer Ceramic Capacitor (MLCC)
- **Capacitance**: 3900 pF (3.9 nF)
- **Voltage Rating**: 50 V DC
- **Capacitance Tolerance**: ±10%
- **Moisture Sensitivity Level**: MSL 1 (JEDEC J-STD-020E)
- **Operating Temperature Range**: -55°C to +125°C
- **Package Type**: 0805 (2.00 x 1.25 mm)
- **Power Consumption**: Not applicable (passive component)
- **Special Features**: 
  - High reliability for industrial applications
  - Suitable for high-frequency applications
  - Low equivalent series resistance (ESR) and inductance (ESL)

#### Description:
The CL21B392KBANNNC is a multilayer ceramic capacitor (MLCC) designed for various electronic applications. It is characterized by its high capacitance value of 3900 pF and a voltage rating of 50 V DC, making it suitable for power management and filtering applications in devices such as smartphones, tablets, and other consumer electronics. The capacitor is constructed using a ceramic dielectric material, which provides excellent stability and reliability under varying temperature and voltage conditions.

#### Typical Applications:
- **Smartphones and Tablets**: Used in power management circuits to stabilize voltage and filter noise.
- **Consumer Electronics**: Employed in audio and video equipment for signal coupling and decoupling.
- **Industrial Equipment**: Suitable for applications requiring high reliability and performance under harsh conditions.
- **DC-DC Converters**: Utilized in power supply circuits to smooth out voltage fluctuations and improve efficiency.

This capacitor is particularly advantageous in applications where space is limited, and high performance is required, such as in modern electronic devices that demand compact and efficient components.
